24:1073:53328:16:17:72:526:398:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sanctioned.  A  detailed  appraisal  report  including  implications  of  such  loan  rescheduling  on 
24:1074:53431:17:17:72:526:381:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the income and other areas of the bank must be placed to the approving authority at the time 
24:1075:53523:17:16:72:252:364:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of placing the rescheduling proposal. 
24:1076:53560:16:17:72:75:348:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
24:1077:53560:17:16:72:526:331:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh  Bank  through  its  BRPD  circulars  issued  at  different  times,  have  announced 
24:1078:53656:16:17:72:523:315:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:various Policy  for  Rescheduling  of  loans,  to  commercial  banks  at  warning  about  non-
24:1079:53750:17:16:72:526:298:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performing  loan.  The  purpose  of  this  Policy for  Rescheduling  of  loans is  to  encourage 
24:1080:53846:16:17:72:526:282:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:commercial  banks  to  accelerate  growth  by  providing  loans  to  these  priority  sectors.  Policy 
24:1081:53949:17:17:72:526:265:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:guidelines and instructions have also been circulated to Commercial Banks for their adoption. 
24:1082:54042:17:16:72:526:248:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Instructions  of, 2006  BRPD  Circular  No.  02  dated  February  14 hereby  stand  superseded 
24:1083:54136:16:17:72:153:232:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by this circular.  
24:1084:54153:17:16:72:75:215:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
24:1085:54153:16:17:72:526:199:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The issue has been reviewed and it has been decided that the borrowers whose credit facility 
24:1086:54246:17:16:72:526:182:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:has  been  rescheduled  will  get  new  loan  facility  subject  to  fulfilment  of  the  following 
24:1087:54346:16:17:72:132:166:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:conditions:- 
24:1088:54358:17:16:72:75:149:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
24:1089:54358:16:17:72:526:133:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a)  The  defaulting  borrower  who  has  availed  interest  waiver  must  settle  at  least  15%  of  the 
24:1090:54464:17:17:72:526:116:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:compromise amount (excluding the down payment on rescheduling as per present guidelines) 
24:1091:54553:17:16:72:312:99:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to avail any further credit facility from any Bank. 
24:1092:54603:16:0:72:75:83:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
24:1093:54603:0:0:106:199:530:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:First Rescheduling 
24:1094:54621:0:14:222:500:537:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Repayment time limit for rescheduling should not exceed 
24:1095:54677:14:14:222:413:523:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:02 years from the date of rescheduling. 
24:1096:54716:14:14:99:461:509:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Second Rescheduling Maximum 01 year from the date of rescheduling. 
24:1097:54781:14:0:103:476:495:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Third Rescheduling Maximum 06 months from the date of rescheduling. 
25:1098:54849:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:b) In case of borrowing from other Banks, the same rule will be applicable, i.e. the borrower 
25:1099:54943:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:will  have  to  settle  at  least  15%  of  compromise  amount  (excluding  the  down  payment  on 
25:1100:55042:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rescheduling  as  per  present  guidelines),  then,  will  be  allowed  to  take  regular  facility  from 
25:1101:55148:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:other   Banks   subject  to  the   submission   of   NOC   (No   Objection   Certificate)   from   the 
25:1102:55251:17:16:72:165:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rescheduling bank. 
25:1103:55269:16:17:72:75:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:1104:55269:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:c) If there  is any Principal waiver, no  fresh  facility will  be allowed till the  full settlement of 
25:1105:55372:17:16:72:176:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:compromise amount. 
25:1106:55390:16:17:72:75:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:1107:55390:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:d) Export  borrowers  may  be  granted  further  credit  facility  (after  being  identified  as  not  a 
25:1108:55494:16:17:72:526:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:willful  defaulter),  if  required,  subject  to  settle  at  least  7.5%  of  the  compromise  amount 
25:1109:55597:17:16:72:479:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(excluding the down payment on rescheduling as per present guidelines) being paid. 
25:1110:55679:16:17:72:75:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:1111:55679:17:17:72:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:e) Prior  approval  of  Bangladesh  Bank  shall  have  to  be  obtained  if  the  loan  is  related  to the 
25:1112:55786:17:16:72:278:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:director/ ex-directors of a Bank Company. 
25:1113:55827:16:17:72:75:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:1114:55827:17:16:72:526:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:f) If  any  such  issue  is  already  there  (such  fresh  facility  has  already  been  allowed  after 
25:1115:55929:16:17:72:412:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:allowing waiver), the same will not fall under purview of this circular. 
25:1116:56001:17:16:72:526:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:06. Information on the loan accounts rescheduled shall be reported to the Credit Information 
25:1117:56094:16:17:72:526:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bureau   (CIB)   of   Bangladesh   Bank.   While   reporting   to   the   CIB,   such   rescheduled 
25:1118:56194:17:16:72:526:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loans/advances  may  be  shown  as  RS  1  for  first  rescheduling,  RS  2  for  second  and  so  on. 
25:1119:56297:16:17:72:526:411:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Interest  waivers  given  to  the  entity  should  be  mentioned  as  RSIW  &  Principal  waivers 
25:1120:56395:17:17:72:266:394:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:granted should be designated as RSPW. 
25:1121:56432:17:16:72:75:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
25:1122:56432:16:11:72:203:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2.7 Review of Literature: 
25:1123:56457:11:14:72:74:350:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
25:1124:56457:14:16:72:525:336:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:Nonperforming loans (“NPLs”) refer  to  those  financial  assets  from  which  banks  no  longer 
25:1125:56554:16:17:72:523:320:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:receive   interest   and/or   installment   payments   as   scheduled.   They   are   known   as   non-
25:1126:56657:17:17:72:526:303:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:performing because the loan ceases to “perform” or generate income for the bank. According 
25:1127:56748:17:16:72:525:286:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:to  Choudhury  et  al.  (2002),  the  nonperforming  loan  is  not  a  “uniclass”  but  rather  a 
25:1128:56846:16:17:72:526:270:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:“multiclass” concept, which means that NPLs can be classified into different varieties usually 
25:1129:56941:17:16:72:526:253:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:based on the “length of overdue” of the said loans. NPLs are viewed as a typical byproduct of 
25:1130:57035:16:17:72:525:237:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:financial  crisis:  they  are  not  a  main  product of  the  lending  function  but  rather  an  accidental 
25:1131:57144:17:16:72:526:220:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:occurrence of the lending process, one that has enormous potential to deepen the severity and 
25:1132:57238:16:17:72:526:204:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:duration of financial crisis and to complicate macroeconomic management (Woo, 2000). This 
25:1133:57328:17:17:72:526:187:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:is  because NPLs can bring down  investors‟ confidence  in the  banking system, piling up 
25:1134:57418:17:16:72:526:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:unproductive economic resources even though depreciations are taken care of, and impeding 
25:1135:57508:16:17:72:526:154:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the resource allocation process. In a bank-centered financial system, NPLs can further thwart 
25:1136:57602:17:16:72:526:137:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economic recovery by shrinking operating margin and eroding the capital base of the banks to 
25:1137:57695:16:17:72:526:121:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:advance new loans. This is sometimes referred to as “credit crunch” (Bernanke et al., 1991). 
25:1138:57788:17:0:72:526:104:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In  addition,  NPLs,  if  created  by  the  borrowers  willingly  and  left  unresolved,  might  act  as  a 
26:1139:57898:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contagious financial malaise by driving good borrowers out of the financial market.1 Further, 
26:1140:57991:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Muniappan  (2002)  argues  that  a  bank  with  high  level  of  NPLs  is  forced  to  incur  carrying 
26:1141:58094:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:costs on non-income yielding assets that not only strike at profitability but also at the capital 
26:1142:58192:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:adequacy  of  a  bank,  and  in  consequence,  the  bank  faces  difficulties  in  augmenting  capital 
26:1143:58295:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:resources. Bonin and Huang (2001) also state that the probability of banking crises increases 
26:1144:58389:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:if financial risk is not eliminated quickly. Such crises not only lower living standards but can 
26:1145:58486:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:also  eliminate  many  of  the  achievements  of  economic  reform  overnight.  The  economic  and 
26:1146:58585:17:16:72:526:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:financial  implications  of  NPLs  in  a  bank-centered  financial  economy can  be  best  explained 
26:1147:58686:16:17:72:199:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by the following diagram. 
26:1148:58711:17:13:72:75:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
26:1149:58711:13:14:72:75:596:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:

26:1171:58816:16:17:72:526:281:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Having such a system, Bangladesh needs to study the condition of NPLs on a routine basis in 
26:1172:58908:17:16:72:526:264:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:order to augment investible capital  in the productive  sectors as well  as to ensure sustainable 
26:1173:59006:16:17:72:167:248:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economic growth.   
26:1174:59024:17:16:72:75:231:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
26:1175:59024:16:17:72:526:215:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The issue of nonperforming loans in Bangladesh is not a new phenomenon. In fact, the seeds 
26:1176:59115:17:17:72:526:198:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:were   cultivated   during   the   early   stage   of   the   liberation   period   (1972-1981),   by   the 
26:1177:59223:17:16:72:526:181:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:government‟s “expansion of credit” policies on the one hand and a feeble and infirm banking 
26:1178:59315:16:17:72:526:165:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:infrastructure combined with an unskilled work force on the other (Islam et al., 1999). Moral 
26:1179:59409:17:16:72:526:148:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:et  al.  (2000)  argue  that  the  expansion  of  credit  policy  during  the  early  stage  of  liberation, 
26:1180:59518:16:24:72:526:132:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:which was directed to disbursement of credit on relatively  easier terms, did actually  expand 
26:1181:59613:24:11:108:75:108:12:Helvetica:6:Times New Roman:                                            1
26:1182:59657:11:12:75:525:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman: If  NPLs  are  not  properly  addressed,  bad  borrowers  can  create  a  negative  psychological  impact  on  good 
26:1183:59773:12:11:72:526:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:borrowers to prolong their payments. This situation becomes worse in an economy where enforcement status of 
26:1184:59881:11:0:72:179:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:laws is seen as very weak.

26:1214:60093:43:0:219:434:326:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:Fig. 2: Economic and financial implications of NPLs 
27:1215:60146:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:credit in the economy on nominal terms. However, it also generated a large number of willful 
27:1216:60239:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:defaulters  in the  background who, later on, diminished the  financial  health of  banks through 
27:1217:60337:17:16:72:526:725:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:the  “sick  industry  syndrome”.2 Islam  et  al.  (1999)  add  that  despite  the  liberalizing  and 
27:1218:60437:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:privatizing  of  the  banking  sectors  in  the  1980s  with  a  view  to  increasing  efficiency  and 
27:1219:60540:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:competition, the robustness of the credit environment deteriorated further because of the lack 
27:1220:60635:16:17:72:526:676:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:of effective lenders‟ recourse on borrowers. Choudhury et al. (1999) find that Government 
27:1221:60725:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:direction  towards  nationalized  commercial   banks  to  lend  to  unprofitable  state  owned 
27:1222:60820:17:16:72:526:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:enterprises, limited policy guidelines (banks were allowed to classify their assets at their own 
27:1223:60917:16:17:72:526:626:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:judgments) regarding “loan classification and provisioning”3, and the use of accrual policies 
27:1224:61011:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of  accounting  for  recording  interest  income  of  NPLs  resulted  in  malignment  of  the  credit 
27:1225:61113:16:17:72:292:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:discipline of the country till the end of 1989.  
27:1226:61161:17:16:72:75:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
27:1227:61161:16:17:72:526:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In  the  1990s,  however,  a  broad  based  financial  measure  was  undertaken  in  the  name  of 
27:1228:61260:17:17:72:526:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:FSRP4, enlisting the help of World Bank to restore financial discipline to the country.  Since 
27:1229:61355:17:16:72:526:526:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:then,  the  banking  sector  has  adopted  “prudential  norms”  for  loan  classification  and 
27:1230:61450:16:17:72:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:provisioning.  Other  laws,  regulations  and  instruments  such  as  loan  ledger  account,  lending 
27:1231:61552:17:16:72:526:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:risk  analysis  manual,  performance  planning  system,  interest  rate  deregulation,  the  Money 
27:1232:61651:16:17:72:526:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Loan Court Act 1990 have also been enacted to promote sound, robust and resilient banking 
27:1233:61741:17:16:72:526:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:practice. Surprisingly, even after so many measures, the banking system of Bangladesh is yet 
27:1234:61834:16:17:72:526:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to free itself from the grip of the NPL debacle. The question thus arises, what are the reasons 
27:1235:61930:17:16:72:526:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:behind  such  a  large proportion of  nonperforming  loans  in the  economy of Bangladesh? Is  it 
27:1236:62028:16:17:72:526:411:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:because of “flexibility in defining NPLs” or lack of effective “recovery strategies” on the part 
27:1237:62125:17:17:72:526:394:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of  the  banks?   Alternatively,   is   it  due  to  poor  enforcement  status  of   laws  related  to 
27:1238:62228:17:16:72:526:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:nonperforming loans? The present study has concentrated on the above issues mainly with a 
27:1239:62318:16:17:72:526:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:view to assisting policymakers to formulate concrete measures regarding sound management 
27:1240:62407:17:17:72:189:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of NPLs in Bangladesh. 
27:1241:62429:17:16:72:75:327:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
27:1242:62429:16:17:72:411:311:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2.8 Base for Provisioning and Accounting Treatment of NPLs: 
27:1243:62487:17:16:72:202:294:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2.8.1 Base for Provision:  
27:1244:62513:16:17:72:521:278:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For eligible collaterals of the following types, provision will be maintained at the stated rates 
27:1245:62611:17:16:72:525:261:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on the outstanding balance of the classified loans less the amount of Interest Suspense and the 
27:1246:62707:16:17:72:203:245:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:value of eligible collateral: 
27:1247:62736:17:16:72:352:228:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a. Deposit with the same bank under lien against the loan, 
27:1248:62794:16:17:72:318:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:b. Government bond/savings certificate under lien, 
27:1249:62844:17:29:72:346:195:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:c. Guarantee given by Government or Bangladesh Bank. 
27:1250:62896:29:7:108:255:166:12:Helvetica:12:Helvetica:                                            
27:1251:62939:7:16:72:525:159:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:2 This  phenomenon  was  observed  in  the  mid-1980s.  This  is  not  a  sunset  industry  but  created  by  borrowers 
27:1252:63058:16:7:72:114:143:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:willfully.  
27:1253:63069:7:16:72:526:136:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:3 Loan classification refers to the process banks use to review their loan portfolios and assign loans to categories 
27:1254:63185:16:12:72:526:120:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:or  grades  based  on  the  perceived  risk  and  other  relevant  characteristics  of  the  loans  (Finance  Forum,  2002). 
27:1255:63310:12:11:72:75:108:10:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman:Provisioning is a method that banks use to set aside funds against possible loan loss. 4
27:1256:63397:11:12:75:525:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:Financial  sector  reform  project  (FSRP)  was  launched  under  financial  sector  adjustment  credit  of  the  World 
27:1257:63517:12:11:72:157:85:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:Bank in early 1990s. 
27:1258:63537:11:0:108:111:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman: 
28:1259:63539:0:16:72:75:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1260:63539:16:17:72:505:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:For all other eligible collaterals, the provision will be maintained at the stated rates on the 
28:1261:63635:17:16:72:378:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:balance calculated as the greater of the following two amounts: 
28:1262:63698:16:17:72:498:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:i. outstanding balance of the classified loan less the amount of Interest Suspense and the 
28:1263:63787:17:16:72:224:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:value of eligible collateral; and 
28:1264:63820:16:17:72:296:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:ii. 15% of the outstanding balance of the loan. 
28:1265:63866:17:17:72:75:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1266:63866:17:16:72:340:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:2.8.2 Accounting of the Interest of Classified Loans: 
28:1267:63919:16:17:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:If any loan or advance is classified as 'Sub-standard' and 'Doubtful', interest accrued on such 
28:1268:64015:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loan  will  be  credited  to  Interest  Suspense  Account,  instead  of  crediting  the  same  to  Income 
28:1269:64121:16:17:72:526:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Account.  In  case  of  rescheduled  loans  the  unrealized  interest,  if  any,  will  be  credited  to 
28:1270:64226:17:16:72:447:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Interest Suspense Account, instead of crediting the same to Income Account.  
28:1271:64302:16:17:72:75:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1272:64302:17:17:72:525:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:As  soon  as  any  loan  or  advance  is  classified  as  'Bad/Loss',  charging  of  interest  in  the  same 
28:1273:64411:17:16:72:526:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:account  will  cease.  In  case  of  filing  a  law-suit  for  recovery  of  such  loan,  interest  for  the 
28:1274:64520:16:17:72:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:period till filing of the suit can be charged in the loan account in order to file the same for the 
28:1275:64620:17:16:72:525:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:amount  of  principal  plus  interest.  But  interest  thus  charged  in  the  loan  account  has  to  be 
28:1276:64726:16:17:72:526:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:preserved  in  the  'Interest  Suspense'  account.  If  any  interest  is  charged  on  any  'Bad/Loss' 
28:1277:64830:17:16:72:526:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:account  for  any  other  special  reason,  the  same  will  be  preserved  in  the  'Interest  Suspense' 
28:1278:64936:16:17:72:525:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:account. If  classified  loan  or  part  of  it  is  recovered  i.e.,  real  deposit  is  effected  in  the  loan 
28:1279:65049:17:16:72:526:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:account,  first  the  interest  charged  and  accrued  but  not  charged  is  to  be  recovered  from  the 
28:1280:65156:16:17:72:342:411:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:said deposit and the principal to be adjusted afterwards. 
28:1281:65213:17:17:72:75:394:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1282:65213:17:16:72:525:377:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:“Making provision  stemmed  from  the  credit  transactions  such  as  credit  sales.  Sales  on  any 
28:1283:65315:16:17:72:526:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:basis  other  than  for  cash  make  possible  the  subsequent  failure  to  collect  the  account.  An 
28:1284:65419:17:16:72:526:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:uncollectable account receivable is a loss of revenue that requires, through proper entry in the 
28:1285:65516:16:17:72:526:328:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:accounts,  a  decrease  in  the  asset  accounts  receivable  and  related  decrease  in  income  and 
28:1286:65618:17:16:72:526:311:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:stockholders‟ equity. Recording the bad debt expense recognizes the loss in revenue and the 
28:1287:65710:16:17:72:526:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:decrease  in  income.  Of  the  two  methods  of  recording  uncollectible  accounts  receivable,  the 
28:1288:65813:17:17:72:526:278:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:allowances  method  is  appropriate  in  situation  where  it  is  probable  that  an  asset  has  been 
28:1289:65917:17:16:72:526:261:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:impaired and that the amount of the loss can be reasonably estimated since the collectability 
28:1290:66011:16:17:72:526:245:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of receivables is considered a loss contingency. A receivable is a prospective cash inflow, and 
28:1291:66106:17:16:72:525:228:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:the probability of its collection must be considered in valuing this inflow (Kieso et al, 2001).” 
28:1292:66203:16:17:72:75:212:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1293:66203:17:16:72:526:195:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:On the other hand, an uncollectable  loan/advance  for the banking  business  is  not only a  loss 
28:1294:66302:16:17:72:526:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of  revenue,  but  also  a  loss  of  capital.  The  uncollectible  interest  receivable  is  the  loss  of 
28:1295:66410:17:17:72:526:162:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:revenue  and  the  uncollectable  principal  is  the  loss  of  capital.  An  analogy  between  the 
28:1296:66510:17:16:72:458:145:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:uncollectable account receivable and the uncollectable interest can be drawn as: 
28:1297:66590:16:17:72:75:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
28:1298:66590:17:16:111:486:112:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Sales price= Cost+ Mark up fir risk premium and profit expectation (spread) 
28:1299:66664:16:0:297:300:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
29:1300:66666:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:So, the provision against the  interest receivable  can  be treated as a normal  business expense 
29:1301:66764:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:since it reflects the probable loss of revenue. The conflict may arise that the nature of banking 
29:1302:66861:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:business is different from the nature of other business and banks are not  utilizing the capital 
29:1303:66958:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:directly to generate revenue-generating goods whereas other business do. But the banks take 
29:1304:67050:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the collateral against the  loans and advances  mainly to create pressure  for timely repayment 
29:1305:67146:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of loans and advances. From this it is evident that the loss of a capital is the fault of either of 
29:1306:67246:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the  legal  system  or  of  the  political  system  of  management  system  but  neither  of  the 
29:1307:67344:17:16:72:526:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:shareholders nor the depositors. Under protectionist banking systems like Bangladesh there is 
29:1308:67438:16:17:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:less chance that the depositors will be deprived in case of a bank failure. So, the loss is of the 
29:1309:67537:17:16:72:184:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:owners (shareholders). 
29:1310:67559:16:17:72:75:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
29:1311:67559:17:16:72:526:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Now a day the bank managers of Bangladesh deduct the amount of interest suspended and the 
29:1312:67649:16:17:72:525:560:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:value of “eligible securities”5 from the outstanding amount in order to determine the base for 
29:1313:67743:17:17:72:526:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:provisioning  to  NPLs.  For  unclassified  loans,  however,  they  keep  a  general  provision  (1%) 
29:1314:67845:17:16:72:526:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:against the outstanding amount and include it in the capital to determine the capital adequacy 
29:1315:67940:16:17:72:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of the bank (at present 9%). With regard to income recognition, as the banking sector follows 
29:1316:68034:17:16:72:526:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:IAS  306 for  preparing  financial  statements,  bank  managers  do  not  consider  the  amount  of 
29:1317:68133:16:17:72:525:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:interest  on  substandard  and  doubtful  loans  as  income  for  the  bank,  but  rather  keep  it 
29:1318:68233:17:16:72:523:460:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:separately in an “interest suspense account”. However, if any amount is received against sub-
29:1319:68326:16:17:72:526:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:standard  and  doubtful  loans,  the  said  amount  is  deducted  from  the  total  interest  suspense 
29:1320:68429:17:16:72:526:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:amount.  In  the  case  of  a  bad/loss  loan,  the  interest  on  such  loan  is  also  kept  in  the  interest 
29:1321:68542:16:17:72:526:411:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:suspense  account  if  a  suit  is  filed  in  the  court.  Seemingly,  with  regard  to  substandard  and 
29:1322:68649:17:17:72:526:394:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:doubtful  loans, this  interest is also excluded  from the  income of the  bank. These accounting 
29:1323:68747:17:16:72:525:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:measures  have  made the  banking sector more transparent and credible than they  were  in the 
29:1324:68842:16:17:72:97:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:past. 
29:1325:68847:17:16:72:75:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
29:1326:68847:16:17:72:75:328:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
29:1327:68847:17:16:72:75:311:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
29:1328:68847:16:17:72:75:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:

29:1336:68890:8:16:72:525:124:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:5 Eligible  securities  include  certificate  of  deposits,  gold  and  gold  ornaments,  government  bonds  /  savings 
29:1337:69009:16:11:72:309:108:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:certificates, easily marketable goods and land & buildings. 
29:1338:69068:11:7:72:75:97:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman: 
29:1339:69068:7:16:72:525:90:6:Times New Roman:10:g_d0_f9:6 IAS stands for International Accounting Standard. IAS 30 deals with the preparation of the bank‟s financial 
29:1340:69177:16:0:72:287:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:statement. Bangladesh adopted this standard in 2000. 
30:1341:69231:0:21:242:325:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Chapter- Three 
30:1342:69244:21:21:153:413:737:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Trend of the Loan Default Problem in Bangladesh 
30:1343:69291:21:17:72:75:716:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
30:1344:69291:17:11:72:212:699:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.1 Nature of the Problem: 
30:1345:69317:11:12:72:74:688:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
30:1346:69317:12:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The  basic  function  of  commercial  banks  is  financial  intermediation  between  savers  and 
30:1347:69414:17:16:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:borrowers.  Banks  are  financial  intermediaries  that  mobilize  funds  from  surplus  economic 
30:1348:69512:16:17:72:526:643:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:units and allocate those funds to deficit economic units. Bank mobilizes fund mainly through 
30:1349:69605:17:16:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:collecting  deposits  and  allocate  those  funds  by  providing  loans.  Bank  credit  is  the  principal 
30:1350:69712:16:17:72:526:610:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sources  of  loanable  fund  for  millions  of  households  and  the  government.  Agricultural, 
30:1351:69809:17:16:72:526:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:commercial,  and  industrial  activities  of  a  nation  are  often  financed  by  bank  credit.  Without 
30:1352:69915:16:17:72:526:577:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:adequate financing there can  be  no growth or  maintenance of stable output.  Thus, the bank 
30:1353:70009:17:17:72:526:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:credit  influences  total  macroeconomic  environment  by  affecting  money  supply,  investment, 
30:1354:70107:17:16:72:222:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:total output, and employment.  
30:1355:70137:16:17:72:291:527:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:                                                                         
30:1356:70209:17:16:72:526:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:This  process  is  an  ongoing  one  that  begins  when  a  loan  application  is  made  and  screened 
30:1357:70312:16:17:72:526:494:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(origination)  and  continues  until  the   loan   is   repaid.   As  unpaid   loans   are   incomplete 
30:1358:70416:17:16:72:527:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:transactions  for  lenders  this  incomplete  transaction  will  not  add  any  value  rather  destroy it. 
30:1359:70523:16:18:72:516:461:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:And this unpaid or default loan causes constraints on the process of economic development.  
30:1360:70613:18:16:72:75:443:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:  
30:1361:70613:16:11:72:242:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.2 Emergence of Default Loans: 
30:1362:70644:11:13:72:74:416:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
30:1363:70644:13:17:72:526:403:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:As  banking  remains  the  main  intermediary  vehicle  of  harnessing  investible  capital  for 
30:1364:70741:17:17:72:526:386:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:accelerating  the  growth  of  the  productive sectors  in  Bangladesh,  the  continuing  crisis  of 
30:1365:70841:17:16:72:526:369:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:accumulation  of  non-performing  and  defaulted  bank  loans  has  emerged  as  one  of  the  most 
30:1366:70941:16:17:72:526:353:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:serious constraints in the path of economic development of our country. Now we will discuss 
30:1367:71033:17:16:72:417:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:how the loan default problem has emerged in our country by year wise. 
30:1368:71101:16:17:72:75:320:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
30:1369:71101:17:11:72:214:303:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.3 Pre Liberation Periods: 
30:1370:71128:11:14:72:74:292:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
30:1371:71128:14:16:72:526:278:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Before the liberalization of Bangladesh , the economic development policies of Pakistan was 
30:1372:71220:16:17:72:525:262:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:centered  around  growth –oriented „modernization paradigm ‟,wherein industrialization was 
30:1373:71311:17:16:72:525:245:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:assigned  the  top  priority  in  the  allocation  of  investible  funds  from  the  institutional  credit 
30:1374:71418:16:17:72:527:229:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sources  in  the  name  of  providing  employment  to  the  vast  multitude  of  the  so-called 
30:1375:71514:17:16:72:526:212:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:„disguisedly  unemployed  labour  force  ‟.This  attempt  of  development  of  an  industrial 
30:1376:71608:16:17:72:526:196:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:entrepreneurial  class  in  Pakistan  miserably  failed  to  provide  adequate  quantum  of  formal 
30:1377:71708:17:16:72:526:179:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:industrial  employment  even  in  West  Pakistan.  This  is  regarded  as  one  of  the  main  factors 
30:1378:71811:16:17:72:526:163:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:behind the rapid growth of „‟regional economic disparity‟‟ between the two Pakistan.  Then 
30:1379:71902:17:17:72:526:146:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banking  was  blamed  as  a  principal  mechanism  of  siphoning –off  capital  from  the  East 
30:1380:71998:17:16:72:526:129:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Pakistan and, therefore, nationalization of the banks and insurance companies, became one of 
30:1381:72091:16:17:72:526:113:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the  most  popular  issues  in  the  election  manifesto  of  the  Awami  League  during  the  1970 
30:1382:72191:17:16:72:172:96:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:election of Pakistan. 
30:1383:72212:16:0:72:75:80:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
31:1384:72214:0:9:72:213:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.4 Post Liberation Period: 
31:1385:72241:9:13:72:73:749:4:Times New Roman:4:Times New Roman: 
31:1386:72241:13:16:72:526:736:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:After the liberation of Bangladesh, the Awami League Government‟s decision to nationalize 
31:1387:72331:16:17:72:526:720:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the  banks  and  insurance  companies  operating  in  Bangladesh  should  be  considered  a  logical 
31:1388:72432:17:16:72:526:703:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:step but the task of re-organization of the nationalized banks in the chaotic, war-ravaged and 
31:1389:72526:16:17:72:526:687:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:crisis-ridden  post-liberation  years  and  a  very  rapid  expansion  of  banking  network  in  rural 
31:1390:72629:17:17:72:526:670:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh   created  some  problems   for  the   banking   sector.  There  was   no  time after 
31:1391:72725:17:16:72:526:653:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:nationalization  as the  most  corrupt,  indisciplined,  overmanned,  and  mismanaged  concerns 
31:1392:72820:16:17:72:526:637:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:mired  in  a  sea  of  recurrent  losses  in  the  backdrop  of  the  political  and  administrative 
31:1393:72921:17:16:72:281:620:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:inexperience of the post liberation regime.  
31:1394:72965:16:17:72:75:604:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
31:1395:72965:17:16:72:525:587:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In  this  scenario,  the  nationalized  banks  were  involved  in  two  sorts  of  pressure  situations, 
31:1396:73070:16:17:72:526:571:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:firstly, the almost insatiable demand  for credit from the  loss  making state-owned enterprises 
31:1397:73167:17:17:72:526:554:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:kept the  banks under constant pressure due to a shortage of adequate  liquidity and  secondly 
31:1398:73262:17:16:72:525:537:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:the  newly emerging so called “briefcase business man” with connection with politics and 
31:1399:73351:16:17:72:526:521:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:politicians,  top  bureaucrats  and  top  bankers,  and  retired  military  and  civil  bureaucrats  were 
31:1400:73457:17:16:72:526:504:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:constantly  lobbing  for  access  to  bank  credit  and  in  the  process  were  vitiating  the  work 
31:1401:73559:16:17:72:526:488:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:atmosphere  in  the  banks  by  alluring  a  section  of  the  bankers  to  indulge  in  corruption  and 
31:1402:73664:17:16:72:526:471:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:malpractices.  It  is  now  widely  recognized  that  today‟s  millionaires  of  Bangladesh  came 
31:1403:73762:16:17:72:526:455:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:mostly from the Ranks of those “briefcase business man” and the groups mentioned,  who 
31:1404:73849:17:16:72:526:438:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:could  successfully  establish  and  maintain  this  types  of  patron  client  relationship  with  the 
31:1405:73953:16:17:72:526:422:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:bankers  and  in  the  process  created  a  host  of  millionaires  from  amongst  those  bankers 
31:1406:74051:17:17:72:525:405:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:themselves,  who  had  actively  connived  and  harvested  the  illicit margins  in  exchange  of  the 
31:1407:74154:17:16:72:300:388:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:favours rationed out to those fortunate loanees. 
31:1408:74202:16:17:72:75:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
31:1409:74202:17:16:72:526:355:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The  political  changes  of  1975  ushered  in  an  era  of  political  culture,  where  in  corruption 
31:1410:74306:16:17:72:526:339:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:gradually became institutionalized, the economics of rent seeking took firm roots in the body 
31:1411:74400:17:16:72:526:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:politic  of  Bangladesh.  In  the  process,  sanctioning  of  bank  loans  became  one  of  the  prime 
31:1412:74503:16:17:72:526:306:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:victims of the buying and selling process afflicting the political party affiliation process, and 
31:1413:74601:17:17:72:526:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a  popular  mechanism  for  doling  out  financial  favors  to  party  leaders  as  well  as  political 
31:1414:74705:17:16:72:526:272:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cadres.  This  politicization  of  the  banking  practices  has  seriously  hampered  the  institutional 
31:1415:74810:16:17:72:526:256:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:disciplines  of  the  banks,  where  professional  expertise,  integrity  and  ethical  values  have 
31:1416:74911:17:16:72:526:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:become exceptions to some extent rather than rules. Ex-bankers emerged as financiers as the 
31:1417:75003:16:17:72:526:223:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:newly  floated  private  banks,  but  there  was  no  mechanism  to  make  them  accountable  or  to 
31:1418:75104:17:16:72:526:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:know about the sources of their cash. Defaulters of bank loans taken from nationalized banks 
31:1419:75197:16:17:72:526:190:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:or  state  owned  development  finance  institutions  swelled  the  rank  of  directors  of  the  newly 
31:1420:75301:17:16:72:526:173:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:established private banks, but nobody intervened on behalf of the loan-giving banks caught in 
31:1421:75395:16:17:72:526:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the middle with defaulted loans. The laws, rules and regulations relating to banking remained 
31:1422:75489:17:17:72:526:140:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:mostly in  the  books;  and  the  judicial  process  utterly  failed  to  take  the  willful  defaulters  to 
31:1423:75598:17:16:72:526:123:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:task, thereby making the process of lender‟s recourse on borrowers almost a mockery in 
31:1424:75685:16:17:72:526:107:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh. Therefore, we surmise that behind all these malaises, the nature of the state and 
31:1425:75779:17:0:72:526:90:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:of politics played the real villainous role by patronizing and developing a class of „comprador 
32:1426:75877:0:16:72:526:758:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:bourgeoisie‟  in  Bangladesh,  created,  nursed  and  constantly  nourished  by  state-patronage. 
32:1427:75975:16:17:72:459:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:And, in this nursing process, bank loans were rampantly used as lucrative doles. 
32:1428:76055:17:16:72:75:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
32:1429:76055:16:17:72:523:709:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:In the eighties, the rapid liberalization of Bangladesh‟s import regime has created the so-
32:1430:76146:17:16:72:526:692:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:called  „sick-industry  syndrome‟,  which  provided  a  potent  excuse  for  some,  and  created 
32:1431:76243:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:genuine hardships regarding repayment of bank loans for the others. The domestic industries 
32:1432:76334:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:have  been  bearing  the  burnt  of  this  ill  advisedly  too  rapid  pace  of  liberalization  of 
32:1433:76434:17:16:72:526:642:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Bangladesh‟s  international  trade  without  appropriate  preparatory  policy  measures.  The 
32:1434:76528:16:17:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:political doldrums of the late-eighties provided additional excuses to these swelling groups of 
32:1435:76624:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:defaulters.  The  BNP  government  of  1991-96  tried  to  stem  the  rot  in  this  field  in  the  initial 
32:1436:76733:16:17:72:526:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:years  of   its  term.  They  repeated  the  blunders  of   its  predecessor  of  providing   lavish 
32:1437:76834:17:16:72:526:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:encouragements  to  bank  managements  to  ease  and  expedite  the  process  of  term  lending, 
32:1438:76931:16:17:72:526:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:especially according to its own political exigencies at the later stages of its rule, which added 
32:1439:77029:17:17:72:526:543:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:a  massive  amount  of  fuel  to  the  fire  of  the  so-called „default-culture‟. And earlier lending 
32:1440:77132:17:16:72:526:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sprees continues to haunt the banking  sector even today  by sustaining the  momentum of the 
32:1441:77225:16:17:72:351:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:build-up of the defaulted loans of the earlier two decades. 
32:1442:77284:17:16:72:75:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
32:1443:77284:16:9:72:395:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:3.5 The Present Status of Loan Default Culture in Bangladesh: 
32:1444:77345:9:13:72:73:468:4:Times New Roman:4:Times New Roman: 
32:1445:77345:13:17:72:526:455:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:As  loans comprise the  most  important asset as well as the primary source of earning  for the 
32:1446:77441:17:16:72:526:438:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banking financial institutions and on the other hand also the major source of risk for the bank 
32:1447:77537:16:17:72:526:422:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:management  so  a  prudent  bank  management  should  always  try  to  make  an  appropriate 
32:1448:77630:17:17:72:525:405:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:balance  between  its  return  and  risk  involved with the loan portfolio. But Banking sector‟s 
32:1449:77727:17:16:72:492:388:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:recent involving activities, guidelines and their concentration in that is not satisfactory. 
32:1450:77819:16:17:72:75:372:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
32:1451:77819:17:16:72:526:355:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:The prudential guidelines also call for making adequate “provisions” against classified loans 
32:1452:77913:16:17:72:525:339:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in order to protect the financial health of the banks are prepared but which is meaningless as 
32:1453:78008:17:16:72:526:322:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:by  making  provision  the  number  of  willful  defaulters  are  increasing  day  by  day.  The 
32:1454:78105:16:17:72:526:306:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:economic implications of the non-performing / default loans are not only stoppage of creating 
32:1455:78199:17:17:72:526:289:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:new  loans  but  also  the  erosion  of  banks  profitability,  liquidity  and  solvency,  which  might 
32:1456:78303:17:16:72:526:272:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sometimes leader towards collapse of the banking financial system. It has, therefore, become 
32:1457:78396:16:17:72:526:256:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sine qua  non  for policy  makers to study the  loan  default  scenario of the  banking  sector of a 
32:1458:78497:17:16:72:526:239:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:routine  basis  for  estimating  classified  loan,  making  appropriate  provisioning,  adopting 
32:1459:78594:16:17:72:524:223:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:effective recovery strategy and thus ensuring soundness and efficiency of the banking sector.  
32:1460:78688:17:16:72:75:206:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
32:1461:78688:16:17:72:526:190:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Before  privatization  and  liberalization  this  banking  activities  were  thus  directed  to  disburse 
32:1462:78794:17:16:72:526:173:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:credit, according to the Government‟s economic priority, and hence little attention was placed 
32:1463:78889:16:17:72:526:157:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to identify the problem loans and making provisions thereon, although there was a significant 
32:1464:78983:17:17:72:525:140:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:amount  of  hidden  default  loans.  After  1982,  the  banking  sector  of  Bangladesh  underwent  a 
32:1465:79085:17:16:72:526:123:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:rapid  denationalization  and  privatization  process.  The  out  of  six  nationalized  commercial 
32:1466:79185:16:17:72:526:107:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:bank (Uttara Bank and Pubali Bank) were denationalized in 1983 and 1984 respectively with 
32:1467:79275:17:0:72:525:90:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:a view to  increasing the  efficiency of the  banking sector. Henceforward, private  banks were 
33:1468:79373:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:allowed  to conduct banking operations ( banking sector books  60 private banks having 628 
33:1469:79464:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:branches,  and  7  foreign  banks  having  14  branches  at  the  end  of  1984)  in  order  to increase, 
33:1470:79570:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:competition, reasons, the efficiency and productivity of the banking sector. But due to various 
33:1471:79666:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:reasons, the efficiency of the banking  sector did  not increase rather the credit discipline was 
33:1472:79764:17:16:72:146:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:further eroded. 
33:1473:79779:16:17:72:75:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
33:1474:79779:17:17:72:525:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The  most  important  aspect  of  this  study  is  to  measure  the  magnitude  of  loans  classified 
33:1475:79881:17:16:72:526:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:substandard,   doubtful   and   bad/loss   since   the   adoption   of   criteria   for   overdue   loan 
33:1476:79986:16:17:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classification in 1990. In connection to this, it must be mentioned that the banking system in 
33:1477:80081:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh  (as  of  December, 2011)  comprises  four  types  of  scheduled  banks – 4  State 
33:1478:80173:16:17:72:525:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:commercial  banks  (SCBs),  5  government-owned  development  financial  institutions  (DFIs), 
33:1479:80268:17:16:72:526:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:30 private commercial banks (PCBs) and 10 foreign commercial banks (FCBs) – for catering 
33:1480:80356:16:17:72:525:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to  the  credit  needs  of the  economy.  Therefore,  data  on  classified  loans  in  both  the  banking 
33:1481:80462:17:17:72:526:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:sector  as  a  whole  and  in  different  clusters  of  banks  are  taken  into  account  to  gain  a  clearer 
33:1482:80573:17:16:72:194:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:picture of the NPL issue. 
33:1483:80598:16:14:72:75:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
33:1484:80598:14:14:72:75:496:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
33:1485:80598:14:13:72:75:482:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:

34:1515:80600:0:21:244:322:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Chapter- Four 
34:1516:80612:21:21:177:390:737:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Loan default status of commercial Banks 
34:1517:80651:21:14:297:300:716:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
34:1518:80651:14:14:297:300:702:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
34:1519:80651:14:8:74:526:688:12:g_d0_f13:12:Times New Roman:4.1 Bangladesh Bank’s Guidelines as per Latest BRPD Circular for Loan Classification  
34:1520:80736:8:12:297:299:680:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
34:1521:80736:12:17:72:526:668:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In  order to  get  rid  of  default  loans  and  to  protect the  bank  capital  from  this  engulfing  crisis 
34:1522:80847:17:17:72:525:651:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the  government  also  formed  a  committee  in  1986  in  the  name  of  National  Commission  on 
34:1523:80946:17:16:72:526:634:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Money,  Banking  and  Credit  for  providing  suggestions  on  non-performing  loans  so  as  to 
34:1524:81043:16:17:72:526:618:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:improve  the  efficiency  of  the  banking  system.  The  Word  Bank  also,  at  this  time  started 
34:1525:81144:17:16:72:384:601:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:making an in-depth study on the financial sector of Bangladesh.   
34:1526:81208:16:17:72:75:585:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
34:1527:81208:17:16:72:526:568:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Regarding the default loans, Bangladesh Bank, however, asked the commercial banks to use 
34:1528:81297:16:17:72:526:552:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:their own subjective criteria for the identification of problem loans and to maintain provisions 
34:1529:81394:17:16:72:526:535:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:against  it.  Therefore,  it  appears  that  the  banking  sector  as  a  whole  simply  neglected  the 
34:1530:81498:16:17:72:526:519:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:identification of problem assets as well as maintenance of proper provision on it. At that time 
34:1531:81594:17:17:72:526:502:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banking community used to believe that they would be able to realize the time bared loans in 
34:1532:81687:17:16:72:526:485:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:full after selling the security kept against it. And as such, they used to deem accrued interest 
34:1533:81783:16:17:72:526:469:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:on the  non-performing  loans as their  income  following the accrual  principles of accounting. 
34:1534:81880:17:16:72:526:452:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Hence,  both  the  profit  and  loss  account  and  the  balance  sheet  did  not  reflect  thee  actual 
34:1535:81985:16:17:72:526:436:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:position and  both  dividend  and  taxes  were  paid  from  the  overstated  income.  This  practice 
34:1536:82085:17:16:72:526:419:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:seriously eroded the capital bases of the banks till the end of 1989, as before that there were 
34:1537:82181:16:17:72:526:403:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:hardly  any  policy  guidelines  by  the  central  bank  regarding  classification  of  loans  and 
34:1538:82280:17:17:72:526:386:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:maintenance of provisions against it. Of course, there was also an absence of appropriate laws 
34:1539:82375:17:16:72:252:369:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:relating to recovery of default loans.  
34:1540:82414:16:17:72:75:353:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
34:1541:82414:17:16:72:526:336:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In order to curb continuing financial distress and to arrest increasing growth of default loans, 
34:1542:82511:16:17:72:526:320:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh  Bank formally  introduced  BCD  Circular  No-34 on  November  16,  1989  on  loan 
34:1543:82604:17:16:72:526:303:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classification  and  making  provisions  thereof.  The  circular  states  that  henceforth  the  banks 
34:1544:82707:16:17:72:526:287:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:themselves will carry out the classifications of their loans at least once in a year on the basis 
34:1545:82805:17:17:72:526:270:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of  the  position  existing  on  December  31  (annual  closing  date)  in  accordance  with  the 
34:1546:82903:17:16:72:526:253:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:guidelines given in the BRPD Circular No. 07 on June 14, 2012: Loan Classification and 
34:1547:82990:16:17:72:526:237:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Provisioning.  It  also  states  that  except  for  agricultural  short-term  loans,  all  loans  are  to  be 
34:1548:83100:17:16:72:526:220:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:classified as either classified' or unclassified‟. Classified loans are to be considered as those 
34:1549:83198:16:17:72:526:204:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loans that have a reduced chance of repayment and are to be further classified as substandard, 
34:1550:83293:17:16:72:526:187:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:doubtful and  bad/  losses. It further states that the bank will use both overdue and qualitative 
34:1551:83390:16:17:72:364:171:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:judgment criteria to deem a loan classified or unclassified.    
34:1552:83453:17:16:72:137:154:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:                      
34:1553:83474:16:17:72:526:138:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:We  know  proper  assessment  of  the  probable  losses  o  revenue  is  required  to  make  proper 
34:1554:83574:17:17:72:526:121:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:provision  and  to  determine  the  net  realizable asset position: “There is always a requirement 
34:1555:83673:17:16:72:526:104:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:for  banks  to  systematically  and  realistically  identify  their  problem  assets  and  provide 
34:1556:83772:16:0:72:526:88:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:adequate reserves for possible losses. To accomplish this, Bangladesh Bank issued guidelines 
35:1557:83867:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in 1989 (vide BCD Circular No. 34, dated 16.11.89) regarding classification and provisioning 
35:1558:83960:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:procedure.  Subsequently,  a  revised  policy  as  introduced  in  1994  (vide  circular  No.20,  dated 
35:1559:84064:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:27.12.94) to be implemented by banks in five phases commencing 31st December 1994. The 
35:1560:84150:16:17:72:525:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:introduction of this program as aimed at bringing loan loss provisioning and classification in 
35:1561:84245:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:line  with  international  standards  by  the  end  of  1998.  Prior  to  1989,  there  were  no  clear  cut 
35:1562:84354:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:policy guidelines to enforce adequate provision by the banks. In the majority of cases, banks 
35:1563:84448:17:17:72:526:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:simply  did  not  identify  problem  assets,  establish  realistic  provisions  for  potential  losses  or 
35:1564:84555:17:16:72:526:642:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:suspend  interest  on  non-performing  assets.  As  a  result,  the  balance  sheet  did  not  reflect  the 
35:1565:84663:16:17:72:526:626:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banks actual condition and the income statement overstated profits upon which dividends and 
35:1566:84755:17:16:72:526:609:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:taxes were paid. However, during the mid-eighties a norm was fixed by Central Bank to raise 
35:1567:84847:16:17:72:526:593:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the  level of provisions  by  0.5% of the total  loans  each  year till  it reached 4%. Obviously,  it 
35:1568:84950:17:16:72:526:576:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:had no relation to loans classified. Interestingly, the banks on the whole did not comply with 
35:1569:85045:16:17:72:526:560:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:this  requirement.  The  situation  ultimately  led  to  unreasonable  developments  regarding 
35:1570:85140:17:17:72:418:543:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:keeping of provisions by the banks (Choudhury et al, 1997, pp.43-44)”. 
35:1571:85210:17:16:72:75:526:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
35:1572:85210:16:17:72:525:510:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:It implies that the Central Bank policy of raising  provision does not cover the  fluctuation  in 
35:1573:85308:17:16:72:526:493:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classified  loan.  Besides  the  commercial  bank  on  the  whole  did  not  comply  with  this 
35:1574:85404:16:17:72:526:477:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:requirement may  be due to luck of Central Bank  supervision,  lack of sufficient profit before 
35:1575:85500:17:16:72:526:460:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:provision  and  taxes.  This  expanse  of  the  borrowers  is  the  interest  against  the  loans  and 
35:1576:85603:16:17:72:526:444:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:advances. For sometimes it is an unavoidable issue that banks charge higher interest rate that 
35:1577:85698:17:16:72:526:427:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:become  difficult  for  the  borrowers  to  repay  and  the  banks  (specially  the  PCBs)  defend 
35:1578:85797:16:17:72:526:411:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:themselves by saying that they have to pay a higher rate against deposits and borrowings, and 
35:1579:85891:17:17:72:526:394:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:they have to add a higher proportion for risk, which actually results from their anticipation of 
35:1580:85988:17:16:72:526:377:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loan loss. Whatever might b e the attack and counter attack, on principle the bank can lose at 
35:1581:86083:16:17:72:526:361:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:most a portion of the interest since interest is the additional amount the borrowers are paying 
35:1582:86179:17:16:72:526:344:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:to the banks for the services they are getting from the banks. How far the reduction of interest 
35:1583:86276:16:17:72:526:328:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:spread, that is, the difference between the interest received and the interest paid will improve 
35:1584:86373:17:16:72:526:311:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:the present bad  loan situation  is  not certain  because willful defaulters are  indifferent to such 
35:1585:86475:16:17:72:105:295:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:steps.  
35:1586:86482:17:17:72:75:278:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
35:1587:86482:17:16:72:527:261:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:4.2 Current Loan Classification and Provisioning System as per Latest BRPD Circular 
35:1588:86566:16:11:72:151:245:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:in Bangladesh: 
35:1589:86580:11:14:72:74:234:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
35:1590:86580:14:16:72:526:220:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Since 1989, Bangladesh follows both “overdue criteria” and “qualitative criteria” to deem a 
35:1591:86672:16:17:72:526:204:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loan  classified  or  unclassified.    According  to  overdue  criteria,  as  suggested  by  Bangladesh 
35:1592:86776:17:17:72:526:187:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bank,  bank  managers  usually  divide  all  loans  into  five  categories  (continuous  loan,  demand 
35:1593:86879:17:16:72:526:170:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:loan,  term  loan  payable  within  five  years,  term  loan  payable  in  more  than  five  years  and 
35:1594:86983:16:17:72:526:154:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:short-term   agricultural   credit   /   micro   credit),   and   then   observe   periods   elapsed   for 
35:1595:87090:17:16:72:526:137:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:repayments.  All  troubled  loans  are  then  further  reclassified  as  special  mention  account 
35:1596:87189:16:24:72:526:121:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(SMA)7,  substandard,  doubtful  and  bad/losses  to  comply  with  international  norms  of  loan 
35:1597:87288:24:7:108:255:97:12:Helvetica:12:Helvetica:                                            
35:1598:87331:7:16:72:525:90:6:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:7 The  special  mention  account  (SMA)  classification  was  introduced  in  Bangladesh  from  the  beginning  of  the 
35:1599:87450:16:0:72:117:74:10:Times New Roman:10:Times New Roman:year 2006. 
36:1600:87462:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:classification. Further, in order to keep the management up to date about the status of  loans, 
36:1601:87558:16:17:72:525:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:bank  managers  review  the  loan  quality  on  a  quarterly  basis.    With  some  exceptions,  the 
36:1602:87659:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:banking  sector  at  present  follows  a  norm  of  six  months  overdue  for  deeming  a  loan 
36:1603:87755:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:nonperforming.    The  rate  of  provision  on  classified  loans  follows  norms  of  5%,  20%,  50% 
36:1604:87857:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and  100%  against  special  mention  accounts,  substandard,  doubtful,  and  bad/loss  loans 
36:1605:87952:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:respectively. The current loan classification and provisioning system (in a summary form) in

38:1878:92491:14:14:72:75:500:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
38:1879:92491:14:16:72:526:486:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:In comparison to the international standard of loan classification and provisioning, it is found 
38:1880:92588:16:17:72:526:470:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:that  the  banking  system  of  Bangladesh  follows  4  stages  (SMA,  sub-standard,  doubtful,  bad 
38:1881:92689:17:17:72:526:453:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:and  loss)  to  define  the  status  of  a  classified  loan,  as  opposed  to  three  stages  (sub-standard, 
38:1882:92799:17:16:72:526:436:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:doubtful,  bad  and  loss)  used  in  the  international  standard.  While  the  international  standard 
38:1883:92904:16:17:72:526:420:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:provides the norm of 3 months overdue for terming a loan substandard, this period is used in 
38:1884:92997:17:16:72:526:403:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:Bangladesh  as  the  norm  for  terming  a  loan  a  “special  mention  account”.  In  addition, 
38:1885:93094:16:17:72:526:387:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh  shows  more  flexibility  than  the  international  standard  in  the  classification  of 
38:1886:93196:17:16:72:525:370:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:long-term  loans. However,  in  the  case  of  provisioning  and  frequency  of  classification, 
38:1887:93292:16:17:72:526:354:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh follows the international standard to a great extent. In the final analysis, it can be 
38:1888:93390:17:17:72:526:337:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:concluded that the present loan classification and provisioning system in use in Bangladesh is 
38:1889:93485:17:16:72:526:320:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:similar  to  a  great  extent  to  the  international  standard,  although  it  is  yet  to  adopt  the 
38:1890:93589:16:17:72:241:304:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:international standard completely.

44:2116:102988:13:17:72:526:352:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:One  of  the  important  aspects  of  the  prudential  norms  of  banking  is  the requirement  of

44:2120:103397:17:16:72:526:285:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:present 2011, the provisioning shortfall of SCBs  is  found to be 14.1%  followed  by PCBs at

44:2122:103584:17:16:72:526:252:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:last  couple  of  years,  although  a  slight  improvement  is  observed  in  case  of  PCBs  (table  7).

46:2168:104759:14:14:168:399:716:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Legal   measures to recover the default loans 
46:2169:104804:14:14:72:75:702:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
46:2170:104804:14:8:72:480:688:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:5.1      EEnnffoorrcceemmeenntt  SSttaattuuss  ooff  LLaawwss  RReellaattiinngg  ttoo  tthhee  DDeeffaauulltt  LLooaannss  iinn  BBaannggllaaddeesshh::    
46:2171:104929:8:14:72:74:680:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
46:2172:104929:14:16:72:526:666:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f9:There is a famous maxim “justice delayed is justice denied”. This can be applied to banks, 
46:2173:105020:16:17:72:526:650:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:especially  in developing  countries  like Bangladesh, owing to the presence of corruption  and 
46:2174:105116:17:17:72:526:633:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:opaqueness in the settlement process as well as poor enforcement of laws that usually create a 
46:2175:105211:17:16:72:526:616:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:fertile ground for the willful defaulters. In the case of Bangladesh, although several laws have 
46:2176:105308:16:17:72:526:600:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:been  enacted and amended with  a  view to ensuring the safety  and soundness of the  banking 
46:2177:105402:17:16:72:525:583:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:system,  the  banking  sector  still  witnesses  an  alarming  amount  of  NPLs.  Therefore,  it  would 
46:2178:105506:16:17:72:526:567:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:be  meaningful  to  measure  the  actual  performance  of  different  courts  in  terms  of  number  of 
46:2179:105610:17:16:72:430:550:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:suits filed, rate of settlement and rate of recovery of NPLs over the years.  
46:2180:105687:16:17:72:75:534:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
46:2181:105687:17:16:72:526:517:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:One  aspect  of  the  study  in  to  evaluate  the  enforcement  status  of  different  lenders  recourse 
46:2182:105793:16:17:72:526:501:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:related  laws.  In  fact,  Bangladesh  has  initiated  legal  reforms  relating  to  banking  since  1972. 
46:2183:105900:17:17:72:527:484:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Since  then,  amendments  have  been  made  in  some  laws  like  Bangladesh  Bank  Order  1972, 
46:2184:105997:17:16:72:526:467:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh  Banks  (Nationalization)  Order  1972,  Negotiable  Instruments  Act  1881,  etc. 
46:2185:106091:16:17:72:526:451:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Again,  some  new  laws  with  prudential  regulations  like  Banking  Companies  Act  1991  and 
46:2186:106188:17:16:72:526:434:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:lenders  recourse  related  laws  like  the  Artha  Rin  Adalat  Ain  2003  and  the  Bankruptcy  Act 
46:2187:106290:16:17:72:526:418:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:1997  have  been  enacted  and  amended  further  with  an  objective  to  ensuring  the  safety  and 
46:2188:106392:17:16:72:526:401:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:soundness  of  the  banking  system.  Therefore,  it  will  meaningful  to  have  a  look  at  the 
46:2189:106491:16:17:72:526:385:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:performance of different courts  in terms of  number of suits  filed, rate of settlement and rate 
46:2190:106589:17:17:72:206:368:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:of recovery over the years.  
46:2191:106617:17:16:72:75:351:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
46:2192:106617:16:11:72:315:335:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:5.2  The Performance of Artha-Rin-Adalat: 
46:2193:106656:11:14:72:74:324:6:Times New Roman:6:Times New Roman: 
46:2194:106656:14:16:72:526:310:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:The Artha  Rin  Adalat  Act  was  enacted  in  1990  to  address  separately  all  issues  related  to 
46:2195:106758:16:17:72:526:294:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:NPLs,  with  the  objective  of  ensuring  the  safety  and  soundness  of  the banking  system.  An 
46:2196:106858:17:17:72:526:277:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:analysis  of  the  performance  of  this  court  reveals  that  the  number  of  suits  filed,  amounts 
46:2197:106962:17:16:72:526:260:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:claimed and number of settled suits have all increased considerably from 1991 to 2011 (table 
46:2198:107055:16:17:72:526:244:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:8). It is also encouraging that the percentage of settled suits has increased considerably from 
46:2199:107151:17:16:72:526:227:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:11.59%  in  1991  to  37.71%  in  2001,  46.36%  in  2004  and  71.69%  in  end  of  2011. 
46:2200:107242:16:17:72:526:211:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Unfortunately,  the  recovery  rate  is  seen  to  be  very  slow  and  is  confined  to  3.65%  in  1991, 
46:2201:107349:17:16:72:526:194:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:8.65%  in  2001  and  19.00%  in  2011,  ultimately  3%-19%  only  during  the  last  twenty  years. 
46:2202:107450:16:17:72:526:178:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Thus,  the  slow  execution  of  the  decrees  in  Bangladesh  can  be  seen  as  the  main  factoring 
46:2203:107553:17:16:72:282:161:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:contributing to very low recovery of NPLs. 
46:2204:107595:16:17:72:75:145:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman: 
46:2205:107595:17:17:72:526:128:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Table 8 (chart 8) shows the overall picture of suits  filed and  settled  in the  Artha Rin  Adalat 
46:2206:107694:17:16:72:526:111:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:during  1991  to  2011.  If  we  focus  our  attention  to  the  bank  group  wise,  it  is  observed  that 
46:2207:107802:16:17:72:526:95:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:number of cases under trial is highest in the SCBs (33796), followed by DFIs (12758), PCBs 
46:2208:107893:17:0:72:526:78:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(10542) and FCBs (179) in 2001 .Though DFIs and PCBs have nearly same number of cases 
47:2209:107981:0:16:72:526:758:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:under  trial,  the  amount  of  suits  under  trial  in  PCBs  is  much  higher  than  DFIs.  In  terms  of 
47:2210:108089:16:17:72:526:742:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:settled cases,  SCBs, DFIs and PCBs all  are having almost equal percentage (about 43%) of 
47:2211:108180:17:16:72:526:725:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cases  settled  while  FCBs  are  far  ahead  of  all  other groups;  the  percentage  of  their  settled 
47:2212:108285:16:17:72:526:709:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:cases  is  70.39%  as  on  June  30,  2000. The  recovery  of  FCBs  is  much  higher  (44.30%)  as 
47:2213:108384:17:16:72:526:692:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:compared  to  SCBs  (8.10%)  and  PCBs  (10.09%).  As  FCBs  operate  under  the  same  legal 
47:2214:108478:16:17:72:526:676:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:framework for loan recovery their far better performance indicate the potential of attaining a 
47:2215:108573:17:17:72:519:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:more effective enforcement than what is so far achieved in regard to SCBs, DFIs and PCBs.

52:2456:115468:14:0:86:197:701:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(CRG) Manual, 2005 
52:2457:115486:0:13:217:514:714:12:g_d0_f11:12:Times New Roman: The credit risk grading system was made mandatory from 
52:2458:115542:13:14:217:515:701:12:Times New Roman:12:g_d0_f9:the  beginning of 2006 to analyze the borrowers‟ credit risk 
52:2459:115603:14:14:217:515:687:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:as well as to prevent fresh NPLs.  In this codified system, if a 
52:2460:115668:14:14:217:515:673:12:g_d0_f9:12:Times New Roman:borrower‟s risk falls within the range of 45-54 out of 100; he 
52:2461:115731:14:13:217:515:659:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:is  not  allowed  to  receive  credit.  Any  borrower  who  has  a 
52:2462:115798:13:15:217:506:646:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:score above the range of 45-54 is eligible to receive credits. 
52:2463:115860:15:14:86:195:631:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Credit Risk Grading 
52:2464:115880:14:0:86:197:617:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:(CRG) Manual, 2007 
52:2465:115898:0:14:217:515:631:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Bangladesh   Bank   vide   its   BRPD   Circular   No.18   dated 
52:2466:115963:14:13:217:515:617:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:December  11,  2005  advised  all  Banks  to  implement  Credit 
52:2467:116027:13:14:217:515:604:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Risk  Grading  for  their  borrowing  clients  as  per  Credit  Risk 
52:2468:116096:14:15:217:302:590:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Grading Manual. 
52:2469:116111:15:13:217:515:575:12:g_d0_f11:12:Times New Roman: If  any  credit  facilities  are  extended  to  a  Bank  against 
52:2470:116177:13:14:217:515:562:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:100%   cash   covered   or   near   cash   covered   securities   or 
52:2471:116246:14:14:217:515:548:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:covered by Government Guarantee or Guarantee by a top tier 
52:2472:116305:14:14:217:515:534:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:International  Bank  then  the  Credit  Risk  Grading  should  be 
52:2473:116371:14:14:217:514:520:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Superior - 1(SUP-1) and in that case the CRG score sheet  is 
52:2474:116430:14:15:217:281:506:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:not required. 
52:2475:116443:15:13:217:515:491:12:g_d0_f11:12:Times New Roman: Key  Risk  Parameters  are  to  be  evaluated  and  weighted 
52:2476:116505:13:14:217:514:478:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:very  carefully,  on  the  basis  of  most  up-to  date  and  reliable 
52:2477:116576:14:14:217:515:464:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:data  and  complete  objectivity  must  be  ensured  to  assign  the 
52:2478:116645:14:15:217:295:450:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:correct grading. 
52:2479:116661:15:13:86:184:435:12:Times New Roman:12:Times New Roman:Financial Stability
